2) The two canonical ladders (the вҖңoctave lawвҖқ that makes it fractal)

4A) Zodiac вҶ’ Hexagram (v1 convention)

Canonical primitives used in this atlas (so вҖңONE unified systemвҖқ is explicit)
P0) The shared substrate: VвӮ„ = в„ӨвӮӮГ—в„ӨвӮӮ (two bits)
Your documents explicitly frame the cross-system basis as the same 2вҖ‘bit structure VвӮ„ вү… в„ӨвӮӮГ—в„ӨвӮӮ, with elemental transformation governed by XOR (Klein four-group operation).

underlying states: {00, 01, 10, 11}
operation: вҠ• = XOR on those 2 bits.
P1) Element labeling is a convention (and you have >1 in the docs)
This matters because your own texts contain two different 00/01 assignments for Water/Earth.
Scheme E_WE (Tarot/Quality Cross scheme):00=Water, 01=Earth, 10=Air, 11=Fire
Scheme E_EW (IвҖ‘ChingвҖ‘aligned scheme, as written in the вҖңHexagram as element-pairsвҖқ section):00=Earth, 01=Water, 10=Air, 11=Fire (this is the alternate labeling that makes вҖң000000 = EarthвҖ‘EarthвҖ‘EarthвҖқ in that section).
Scheme E_BIN (binary-order scheme in Astrological Tunneling):00=Air, 01=Fire, 10=Water, 11=Earth
О© consequence: whenever a mapping depends on elementвҶ”bits naming, it is at least NEAR, unless we explicitly fix the scheme.
P2) Hexagram as 3 element-pairs (Root / Expression / Mode)
Your unified divination text gives a direct structural encoding:
Lines 1вҖ“2 = ROOT element
Lines 3вҖ“4 = EXPRESSION element
Lines 5вҖ“6 = MODE element
вҖҰand it treats a hexagram as 6 bits (consistent with 2вҒ¶=64).

Your notes said: define the trigger predicate and seam completions (30/90/360) so scaling becomes governed recursion.Here is the exact carry law:
TCR: one decan tick update
Decan step
(d \leftarrow d+1 \pmod 3)
If decan overflows (30В° seam), carry into sign

ThatвҖҷs it. Triangle digits overflow upward; the circle wrap count is base-3; the carry events are your seam triggers.

Deterministic I/O bit from TF-ADDR
Define:
sextile sector index (u = \big\lfloor (30s)/60 \big\rfloor = \lfloor s/2 \rfloor)
parity inside sextile sector (p = s \bmod 2) (first sign vs second sign)
Then the sign splits:
if (p=0): 20В° + 10В° (Input then Output)
if (p=1): 10В° + 20В° (Input then Output)
At decan resolution (d\in{0,1,2}), the I/O rule is:
if (p=0): Input when (d\in{0,1}), Output when (d=2)
if (p=1): Input when (d=0), Output when (d\in{1,2})
So:[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=\textsf{IO}(s,d)\in{0,1}}]
Then the elder index is literally:[\boxed{E = 2s + \textsf{IO} + 1 \in {1,\dots,24}}]This is the computable object behind вҖң24 = 12Г—2 = input/output.вҖқ

Discriminator Menus v3 вҖ” standardized collapse operators (AMBIGвҶ’NEARвҶ’OK)
This is the engineвҖҷs вҖңhow to stop ambiguityвҖқ table. It is intentionally small: a few primitive discriminators collapse almost everything.
D0) Core collapse primitives (the only ones you need)
AddAnchor: add a witnessed modular constraint (n\equiv a\ (\bmod m)) вҶ’ reduces CrossCal ambiguity.
ExtraCast(bits=k): generate k missing bits (k=1 for 128, k=2 for IfГЎ refinement).
PinGauge: choose and pin the codec convention (element labeling / ordering) so replay is stable.
ShiftWindow(ВұО”t): if two candidates differ by a nearby seam/node, shift the time window slightly and recompute О”; one candidate will stabilize (node proximity test).
ObserveManifest: a minimal real-world observation collapses Active/Passive when youвҖҷre at 256 (manifest vs latent).
D1) CrossCal / Chronometry ambiguity
AMBIG cause: multiple offset candidates / Оһ-family underdetermined
Candidate set: ({(o_i)}) offset bundles + residual ledger
Collapse: AddAnchor or ShiftWindow until residual ledger discriminates
Promotion rule: AMBIGвҶ’NEAR once one candidate dominates residual bounds; NEARвҶ’OK once witness+replay closure passes
D2) I-Ching вҶ’ IfГЎ refinement (64вҶ’256)
AMBIG cause: lossy projection inversion (each hexagram has 4 substates)
Candidate set: ({4\cdot \text{HexIdx}+0..3})
Collapse: ExtraCast(bits=2) OR apply PhaseГ—Mode discriminator (arr/dep Г— act/pass)
Promotion: OK if suffix bits are witnessed (cast receipts pinned)
D3) Whole-nakshatra вҶ’ decan
AMBIG cause: nakshatra spans multiple decans unless pada/degree known
Candidate set: {dom, tail} (3 padas vs 1 pada)
Collapse: AddDegree (equivalently: determine pada) вҶ’ OK via the 108вҶ’36 bridge
D4) RuneвҶ’Major / MajorвҶ’Rune
AMBIG cause: operator overlap (multiple runes witness same major)
Candidate set: rune set per major (and vice versa)
Collapse: PinDomain (ГҶtt/domain) + optionally ExtraCast(bits=1) for tie-break
Promotion: OK within pinned domain convention
D5) 128 derivative bit (static/dynamic) when not measured
NEAR cause: derivative inferred from IO/seam proximity rather than cast
Candidate set: {static, dynamic}
Collapse: ExtraCast(bits=1) OR direct I-Ching moving-line measurement
D6) 256 active/passive bit when not measured
AMBIG cause: latent vs manifest not observable from structure alone
Candidate set: {active, passive}

A codec should not fight this:
When DerivBit is measured (oracle), it overrides geometry.
When DerivBit is not measured, IO/seam proximity can only be NEAR.

Operationally: minimize average Hamming distance between successive tiles under your carry rule.

Time Fractal System v3.2 вҖ” K-table canon + IO extraction from (u,j)
1) 12Г—18 overlay вҶ’ 24 tiles (hard geometry, pinned)
Inside each 60В° macro-arc, the overlay boundaries are always:[{0,20,30,40,60}]so the tile index (j\in{0,1,2,3}) corresponds to:
(j=0:\ [0,20))
(j=1:\ [20,30))
(j=2:\ [30,40))
(j=3:\ [40,60))
Repeated across 6 macro-arcs вҶ’ 24 tiles.
Define:
(u=\left\lfloor \theta_{\text{base}}/60\right\rfloor\in{0,\dots,5})
(r=\theta_{\text{base}}-60u\in[0,60))
(j=\begin{cases}0 & r<20\1 & 20\le r<30\2 & 30\le r<40\3 & 40\le r<60\end{cases})
Then the 24-tile index is:[\boxed{\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1}](1-indexed).
2) IO bit and Elder index вҖ” purely from (u,j)
RevelationвҖҷs architectural meaning is explicit:[24 = 12\times 2 = \text{Input cycle} + \text{Output cycle}]
Now the key closure: each 30В° sign is exactly two overlay tiles inside its 60В° macro-arc:
sign A (first 30В°) uses tiles (j=0,1)
sign B (second 30В°) uses tiles (j=2,3)
So you can recover sign index (s\in{0..11}) directly:[\boxed{s=2u+\left\lfloor j/2\right\rfloor}]
And the Input/Output bit is simply:[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2}]
even (j) = Input
odd (j) = Output
Then the Elder index (12Г—2) becomes:[\boxed{\textsf{Elder}=2s+\textsf{IO}+1}]
Substitute (s=2u+\lfloor j/2\rfloor) and (\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2), you get:[\textsf{Elder}=4u+j+1]
So:
[\boxed{\textsf{Elder}=\textsf{Tile24}}]
That is the cleanest unity statement in the entire build: the 24 overlay tiles are the 24 elders (tile index is the elder index), with IO as the parity bit.
О© status:
Geometry + formulas above are OK (pure overlay arithmetic).
вҖңInput/OutputвҖқ semantics are OK inside the pinned IO convention, with Revelation as the witness for the doubling meaning.
3) K-table canon (the last missing pin for the overlay-aware hex codec)
You already pinned the hex line-pair decoder:
11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 Earthand hex layout:
(1вҖ“2)=Root, (3вҖ“4)=Expression, (5вҖ“6)=Mode
Now we pin the overlay mixer constants.
3.1 K(IO) вҖ” minimal Hamming toggle (canonical)
We want InputвҶ’Output inside the same sign to change the hex core in the smallest possible way (smooth flow constraint; avoids pseudo-random jumps). Since pair codes are 2 bits, the minimal toggle is XOR with a 1-bit mask.
Canon:
(\boxed{K(0)=00}) (Input: no twist)
(\boxed{K(1)=01}) (Output: flip 1 bit)
So:[\boxed{K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}}]
Why this choice is structurally вҖңbestвҖқ:
switching IO changes ExpressionPair by Hamming distance 1 (controlled minimal delta).
О© status: OK (pinned definition).
3.2 Optional fractal constant K(tвӮҖ) (wrap-trit mixer)
Triangle scaling is base-3 in the circle: (360\cdot 3^n).So the first wrap trit (t_0\in{0,1,2}) is the natural вҖңfractal textureвҖқ selector.
Canon:
(K(0)=00)
(K(1)=10)
(K(2)=11)
This gives a monotone вҖңpowerвҖқ feel (0,2,3 in bit-weight) and avoids mapping two trits to the same 2-bit constant.
О© status: OK (pinned definition).

1) GaugePin v3.3 вҖ” TF-ADDR вҶ’ Root/Mode is now explicit
1.1 Canonical pair decoder (already pinned)
Hex line-pair decoder is fixed:
11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 EarthHex layout is fixed:
(1вҖ“2)=Root, (3вҖ“4)=Expression, (5вҖ“6)=Mode
So вҖңRootPairвҖқ and вҖңModePairвҖқ are literally 2-bit values in ({00,01,10,11}).
1.2 BaseElement(s): Zodiac element gauge (pinned)
Your astrological module explicitly defines signs in an element:mode format (e.g., Aries = Fire:Fire, Taurus = Earth:Water, etc.).
From that, the canonical base element pattern is the standard repeating cycle over sign index (s\in{0..11}):[\textsf{BaseElement}(s)=\begin{cases}\text{Fire} & s\equiv 0\ (\bmod 4)\\text{Earth} & s\equiv 1\ (\bmod 4)\\text{Air} & s\equiv 2\ (\bmod 4)\\text{Water} & s\equiv 3\ (\bmod 4)\end{cases}](Aries Fire, Taurus Earth, Gemini Air, Cancer Water, вҖҰ)
Then:[\boxed{\textsf{RootPair}=\textsf{ElemPair}(\textsf{BaseElement}(s))}]using the fixed decoder table.
1.3 ModeElement(П„): modality gauge (Triangle вҶ’ mode-element) (pinned)
Your modality recode is explicit:
Cardinal = Fire-mode
Fixed = Water-mode
Mutable = Air-mode
Since zodiac modalities repeat every 3 signs, we can set:[\tau = s \bmod 3]and map:[\textsf{ModeElement}(\tau)=\begin{cases}\text{Fire} & \tau=0\ \ (\text{Cardinal})\\text{Water} & \tau=1\ \ (\text{Fixed})\\text{Air} & \tau=2\ \ (\text{Mutable})\end{cases}]
Then:[\boxed{\textsf{ModePair}=\textsf{ElemPair}(\textsf{ModeElement}(\tau))}]again using the fixed decoder.
This is the вҖңSquareГ—Triangle inside CircleвҖқ kernel made literal: (s\leftrightarrow(e,\tau)\in\mathbb{Z}_4\times\mathbb{Z}_3) (12=4Г—3).
2) OverlayвҶ’IO is now purely (u,j) (hard lock)
The 12Г—18 overlay micro-structure is hard:within each 60В° sector, the tiles are ([0,20),[20,30),[30,40),[40,60)) and repeat 6Г— вҶ’ 24 tiles.
Define:
(u=\lfloor\theta/60\rfloor\in{0..5})
(j\in{0,1,2,3}) by which subinterval (\theta) is in
Then:[\boxed{\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1}]
RevelationвҖҷs meaning of doubling is explicit:[24=12\times 2=\text{Input cycle + Output cycle}]
So we set:[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2}]and the elder index becomes:[\boxed{\textsf{Elder}=4u+j+1=\textsf{Tile24}}](geometry index and elder index coincide under the pinned I/O semantics).
3) Codec v3.3-B вҖ” TF-ADDR вҶ’ Hex64 is now replay-deterministic
We keep the overlay-aware family member you built, but now Root/Mode are pinned (so вҖңNEARвҖқ collapses to вҖңOKвҖқ once gauge pins are declared in the capsule).
3.1 K(IO) canon (minimal toggle)
[K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}](so toggling IO flips 1 bit in Expression вҖ” smoothest possible local change).
3.2 Hex core construction
[\boxed{\textsf{ExprPair}=\textsf{RootPair}\ \oplus\ \textsf{ModePair}\ \oplus\ K(\textsf{IO})}]and[\boxed{\textsf{HexBits}=\textsf{RootPair}\ |\ \textsf{ExprPair}\ |\ \textsf{ModePair}}]Hex layout is exactly Root/Expr/Mode pairs.
So every time address produces a 64-state node as a triple of element-pairs (which is exactly how your hexagram encoder is defined).
4) 64-Mansion Graph GвӮҶвӮ„ вҖ” from вҖңstate spaceвҖқ to вҖңtime dynamicsвҖқ
Your time system explicitly treats 64 as a state space and discusses movement rules driven by changes (moving lines / change count).Your unified divination layer also pins:
128 = 64Г—2 as the derivative bit (static/dynamic; positionГ—velocity)
and aligns that derivative bit across interfaces (I-Ching moving lines вҶ” Tarot reversals вҶ” rune merkstave).Your 256 layer is PhaseГ—Mode with exact numbering.
So we define the 64-graph as:
Vertices: (V={0,1}^6) (or equivalently ({00,01,10,11}^3) in pair-chunks).
Edges: induced by a small operator set, each operator corresponding to a lawful вҖңcause of changeвҖқ in your engine.
4.1 Operator basis (the minimum set)
Represent a node as:[H=(R,E,M)\quad \text{where }R,E,M\in{00,01,10,11}]and (H) corresponds to 6 bits via concatenation.
OвӮҖ: DriftStep (time carry)
compute next TF-ADDR by the carry rule (10В° tick)
recompute IO and then recompute (H) via codec
This gives you the deterministic вҖңclock walkвҖқ on GвӮҶвӮ„.
OвӮҒ: IOFlip (tile parity toggle)When (j) flips parity (IO toggles), ExpressionPair toggles by XOR with 01:[(R,E,M)\mapsto (R,\ E\oplus 01,\ M)]This is the micro-motion caused by the 12Г—18 overlay itself.
OвӮӮ: ChangeLine (oracle-driven line flip)When moving lines are measured, you apply the standard вҖңchange lines вҶ’ new hexagramвҖқ operator.Your system explicitly treats вҖңmovementвҖқ as driven by change count and changing lines rather than treating 64 as a static list.
This operator is not вҖңtime driftвҖқ; itвҖҷs вҖңoracle derivative.вҖқ It is exactly why 128 exists.
OвӮғ: SubstateRefine (256 refinement)Given a hex core, PhaseГ—Mode bits refine into 4 substates with the explicit numbering:[\textsf{State256}=(\textsf{HexIdx}\times 4)+(\textsf{Phase}\times 2)+\textsf{Mode}]
5) Transition weights вҖ” how вҖңtime weatherвҖқ becomes a probabilistic kernel
You asked for вҖңtransition weights from carry events + seam proximity.вҖқ Here is the engine-native way to do it:
5.1 Features (all computable from TF-ADDR + CrossCal nodes)
Define seam distances:
(\Delta_{30},\Delta_{60},\Delta_{90},\Delta_{360}) (distance to nearest seam family)and node distance:
(\Delta_{\text{node}}) (distance to nearest LCM/CRT window from CrossCal).
Define derivative flag (if measured):
DerivBit вҲҲ {0 static, 1 dynamic}
Define phaseГ—mode bits (if measured/refined):
arriving/departing Г— active/passive
5.2 Weight functions (simple, monotone, seam-driven)
Use any monotone map (g(\Delta)) with:
(g(0)=1)
(g(\Delta)\downarrow 0) as (\Delta\uparrow)
Then define operator weights:
wвӮҖ (drift): always on
wвӮҒ (IOFlip): proportional to (g(\Delta_{20/30/40})) вҖ” but since IO is directly tied to tile parity, you can just treat this as deterministic when crossing tile boundaries.
wвӮӮ (oracle change): depends on DerivBit
if static (0), wвӮӮ is near 0
if dynamic (1), wвӮӮ is high(this is exactly вҖң128 = positionГ—velocityвҖқ in your system).
wвӮғ (tunnel emphasis near nexus seams): proportional to (g(\Delta_{60})) because the 60В° lattice is your shared synchronization substrate (the overlay itself is built on it).
w_node (alignment emphasis): proportional to (g(\Delta_{\text{node}})), because node windows are where multiple cycles phase-lock.
5.3 Markov kernel form (what вҖңweighted walkвҖқ means)
Let (H_t) be the current 64 node. Define a set of candidate next nodes by applying operators:[\mathcal{N}(H_t)={O_i(H_t)}]Then:[P(H_{t+1}=y\mid H_t)\ \propto\ \sum_i w_i\cdot \mathbf{1}[y=O_i(H_t)]]Where:
if you have a measured moving-line set, (O_2) is a single or small set of concrete flips (OK)
if you donвҖҷt, (O_2) becomes a candidate family (AMBIG) and must carry a discriminator plan (extra cast / observation).
This is the exact formal meaning of вҖңtime weatherвҖқ: a local transition kernel on the 64 state space whose weights are modulated by seams and alignments.
6) How this integrates 128 and 256 cleanly (no handwaving)
6.1 128 derivative bit controls operator mixture
DerivBit=0: drift dominates (time is вҖңstickingвҖқ in the current regime)
DerivBit=1: change-line operator gets weight (time is вҖңtransitioningвҖқ)
ThatвҖҷs literally positionГ—velocity.
6.2 256 substate controls вҖңmanifestation energyвҖқ
When you have the 256 refinement, you can tie:
arriving vs departing вҶ’ sign of the derivative
active vs passive вҶ’ whether changes express externally or remain latent
And because the 256 numbering rule is explicit, you can store the refined state without ambiguity when measured.
7) The final closure of v3.3 (what you now have)
You now have a single closed loop:
CrossCal produces (n,\Theta_{total}) and node windows (alignment gates).
TF-ADDR extracts ((s,d,u,j)) and seam distances.
Overlay gives IO and elder/tile index deterministically.
GaugePin maps TF-ADDR вҶ’ RootPair/ModePair (no ambiguity).
Codec maps вҶ’ Hex64 (Root/Expr/Mode triple).
128/256 bits refine the state and control transition weighting.
The вҖңtime weatherвҖқ is a weighted walk on the 64 mansion graph, driven by carry events + seam proximity + nodes + derivative bits.

Time Fractal System v3.4 вҖ” Carry-Event вҶ’ Operator Schedule
Closed-form updates for (R,E,M) so the 64-walk is simulable from time-address alone (oracle becomes optional overlay)
0) The pinned primitives this schedule depends on
0.1 12Г—18 overlay micro-geometry (gives 24 tiles)
Within any 60В° sextile sector, the 12-grid bins are ([0,30),[30,60)) and the 18-grid bins are ([0,20),[20,40),[40,60)). Their intersections are always:[[0,20),\ [20,30),\ [30,40),\ [40,60)]with widths (20В°,10В°,10В°,20В°), repeated six times вҶ’ 24 joint tiles.
0.2 Hex64 representation (what (R,E,M) means)
Hexagram is read as three element-pairs:
Lines 1вҖ“2 = ROOT
Lines 3вҖ“4 = EXPRESSION
Lines 5вҖ“6 = MODE
Line-pair decoding (Yang/Yin):
11 Fire, 10 Air, 01 Water, 00 Earth
So the 64-node вҖңmansion stateвҖқ is:[H=(R,E,M)\in{00,01,10,11}^3]
0.3 Triangle scaling carry seams (when вҖңgoverned recursionвҖқ triggers)
Your triangle carry rule is explicitly tied to seam completions:
end of octave (360)
end of element block (90 base / 270 meta)
end of decan triplet (30 base / 90 meta)and a trigger predicate template is given:[\text{Trigger}(\theta)=1\iff \theta\in{0,30,90,180,270,360}\ (\bmod 360)]
1) Extract the tile address (u,j) from base phase Оё
Let (\theta\in[0,360)) be base phase (after Phase(Lift(В·))). Triangle scaling preserves phase but increases wrap count, so this extraction is octave-stable.
Compute:
sextile sector: (u=\lfloor \theta/60\rfloor\in{0,1,2,3,4,5})
local sector angle: (r=\theta-60u\in[0,60))
tile-in-sector:[j=\begin{cases}0 & 0\le r<20\1 & 20\le r<30\2 & 30\le r<40\3 & 40\le r<60\end{cases}](This is exactly the 12Г—18 intersection partition.)
Define the IO bit (purely from tile parity):[\boxed{\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2}]and (optional) the 24-tile index:[\textsf{Tile24}=4u+j+1](24 joint tiles).
2) Extract the sign skeleton (base element + modality вҶ’ internal mode)
You already formalized вҖң12 archetypes = Element Г— ModalityвҖқ and then upgraded Modality into an internal mode-triad (init/hold/shift).
2.1 Sign index from the overlay
Inside each sextile sector, the first 30В° half is the first sign and the second 30В° half is the second sign. From the tile index:[\boxed{s = 2u + \left\lfloor j/2\right\rfloor}\quad \in{0,\dots,11}]This agrees with the partition ([0,30)) vs ([30,60)) in each sector.
2.2 Base element and modality of sign
Your sign table explicitly pairs each sign with its element and modality (Cardinal/Fixed/Mutable).Equivalently, modality is the triad:
Cardinal = initiate
Fixed = stabilize
Mutable = adapt/transform
2.3 ModeElement (the internal triad mapping you defined)
You explicitly set:
Cardinal = Fire-mode
Fixed = Water-mode
Mutable = Air-mode
So:[\textsf{ModeElement}(s)=\begin{cases}\text{Fire} & \text{if Modality(s)=Cardinal}\\text{Water} & \text{if Modality(s)=Fixed}\\text{Air} & \text{if Modality(s)=Mutable}\end{cases}]
3) Define K(IO) (the only extra pin needed for overlay-aware hex)
We need one tiny constant table to let IO modulate the hex core with minimal delta:
[K(\textsf{IO})=\begin{cases}00 & \textsf{IO}=0\01 & \textsf{IO}=1\end{cases}]
This means IO toggling flips exactly 1 bit in the ExpressionPair (smoothest possible change).
4) The deterministic Hex64 codec (time-address вҶ’ (R,E,M))
Let enc(element) map to 2-bit pair via the fixed decoder (Fire=11, Air=10, Water=01, Earth=00).
Define:
(R = \textsf{RootPair} = enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s)))
(M = \textsf{ModePair} = enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s)))
Then the overlay-aware expression pair is:[\boxed{E = R\ \oplus\ M\ \oplus\ K(\textsf{IO})}](where (\oplus) is bitwise XOR on 2-bit strings; this is the canonical group operation for the 2-bit element space).
And the 64-state node is:[\boxed{H(\theta)=(R,E,M)}]with (R,E,M) exactly corresponding to (Root/Expression/Mode) line-pairs.
Key simplification from the overlay:Because (\textsf{IO}=j\bmod 2), every tile parity flip produces a controlled (E) flip, while (R,M) only change when (s) changes.
5) Carry-Event вҶ’ Operator Schedule (exact, event-by-event)
We evolve (\theta) in 10В° decan ticks (base). Triangle scaling turns this into (10В°\to 30В°\to 90В°\to\cdots) ladders across octaves, but the base phase extraction is the same.
Let the step be (\theta^+ = (\theta + 10В°)\bmod 360). Compute ((u,j,s,\textsf{IO})) at (\theta) and (\theta^+). Then classify the event:
Event types
EVT-0: HOLD (no tile boundary crossed)
Condition: (j^+=j)
Operator fired: O_hold
Update:[(R^+,E^+,M^+)=(R,E,M)]
EVT-1: IO-FLIP (20В° or 40В° boundary)
Condition: (s^+=s) but (\textsf{IO}^+\ne \textsf{IO})This occurs exactly at (r=20) and (r=40) boundaries inside the 60В° sector, i.e. (j) flips parity but (\lfloor j/2\rfloor) stays the same.
Operator fired: O_IOFlip
Update (closed-form):[R^+=R,\quad M^+=M,\quad E^+=E\oplus 01]because (K(\textsf{IO})) toggles between 00 and 01.
EVT-2: SIGN-STEP (30В° boundary)
Condition: (s^+=s+1) with the same sextile sector (u^+=u)This happens at the (r=30) boundary where we move from the first 30В° bin to the second 30В° bin.
Operator fired: O_signAdvance(also this is one of your вҖңdecan triplet completionвҖқ lift triggers: 30В° seam is in the trigger set).
Update:
recompute (R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s^+)))
recompute (M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s^+)))
compute (E^+=R^+\oplus M^+\oplus K(\textsf{IO}^+))
Shortcut: at a sign boundary in this overlay, the landing tile is always (j^+=2) (even), so (\textsf{IO}^+=0), hence:[\boxed{E^+=R^+\oplus M^+}]
EVT-3: SEXTILE-STEP (60В° boundary)
Condition: (u^+=u+1) (wrap mod 6), i.e. crossing the sextile hub set (\theta\in{0,60,120,180,240,300}).
Operator fired: O_sextileAdvanceThis is both:
a sign step (from the second sign of one sector to the first sign of the next),
and a hub checkpoint (the вҖңnexus pointsвҖқ).
Update:
(s^+=s+1) (mod 12)
landing tile is (j^+=0) (even), so (\textsf{IO}^+=0)
therefore:[\boxed{R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(s^+)),\quad M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(s^+)),\quad E^+=R^+\oplus M^+}]
EVT-4: ELEMENT-SEAM (90В° checkpoint)
Condition: (\theta^+\in{0,90,180,270}) (mod 360)This is explicitly a вҖңlegal lift pointвҖқ seam family (90В° base / 270В° meta) in your triangle carry spec.
Operator fired: O_quarterCheckpoint (no change to H by itself)
Update:[(R^+,E^+,M^+) \text{ as determined by whichever of EVT-0..3 occurred, plus log checkpoint flag}]
EVT-5: OCTAVE-WRAP (360В° boundary)
Condition: (\theta^+\equiv 0) (mod 360)This is the вҖңend of octaveвҖқ seam and is explicitly in the carry-trigger list.
Operator fired:
O_wrapCarry (increment the wrap-trit tower; triangle scaling is the Г—3 wrap-count lift).
Update of H at base phase is just the sextile/sector logic (it lands at (\theta=0\Rightarrow u=0,j=0,s=0,\textsf{IO}=0)), so:[R^+=enc(\textsf{BaseElement}(0)),\quad M^+=enc(\textsf{ModeElement}(0)),\quad E^+=R^+\oplus M^+]and separately you carry (w) (wrap index) in base-3 digits.

7) Optional: deterministic 128/256 overlays from the same schedule (oracle remains measurement overlay)
7.1 128 вҖңvelocityвҖқ bit (geo-proxy)
Your text defines the 7th bit as temporal phase: Static (0) vs Dynamic (1), with Static = crystallizing/arriving and Dynamic = transforming/departing.
A purely time-address proxy is:[\textsf{DerivBit}_\text{geo}=\begin{cases}0 & j^+=j \ (\text{no boundary crossed})\1 & j^+\ne j \ (\text{boundary crossed})\end{cases}]This converts the carry schedule into вҖңmoving vs not movingвҖқ without any oracle input.
7.2 256 PhaseГ—Mode (geo-proxy)
Your 256 structure is explicitly:
Phase: Arriving (0) vs Departing (1)
Mode: Active (0) vs Passive (1)and State# = HexIdxГ—4 + PhaseГ—2 + Mode.
A clean deterministic proxy consistent with the 128 semantics is:
PhaseBit_geo = DerivBit_geo (0 arriving, 1 departing)
ModeBit_geo = 0 when in the narrow 10В° tiles (j=1 or 2), 1 when in the wide 20В° tiles (j=0 or 3)(because the microstructure explicitly distinguishes 20В° vs 10В° cells).
Oracle measurements (moving line data; extra casts) can override these proxies and promote truth status (your system already treats measured dynamic as the true derivative bit).
8) Minimal simulation algorithm (text, step-by-step)
Start with (\theta_0) and choose octave depth (n). Compute (\theta=\textsf{Phase}(\textsf{Lift}(\theta_0,n))).
Extract ((u,j)) from (\theta) using the 12Г—18 micro-intervals.
Compute (s=2u+\lfloor j/2\rfloor), IO = j mod 2.
Compute RootElement and Modality from sign table (ElementГ—Modality = 12).
Convert ModalityвҶ’ModeElement via your internal triad (CardinalвҶ’Fire, FixedвҶ’Water, MutableвҶ’Air).
Encode Root/Mode into 2-bit pairs using the pinned hex decoder.
Compute ExpressionPair = Root вҠ• Mode вҠ• K(IO).
Advance by 10В° and repeat; event classification tells you which operator fired (hold / IO flip / sign advance / sextile / quarter / octave).

2.2 The change operator: вҖңmoving linesвҖқ = legal jump generator
Your state-space spec is explicit: changing lines define which hexagram you move to, and the number of changing lines controls the Hamming distance.
So define:
(L\subseteq{1,\dots,6}) = set of changing lines at time t
(H^{\text{chg}}_{t+1} := H_t \oplus \textsf{Mask}(L)), where Mask(L) flips the selected line bits.
This exactly implements:
|L|=0 вҶ’ stay
|L|=k вҶ’ move to hex that differs by k lines
2.3 The 128 layer: the derivative bit controls whether change operators fire

So:[\boxed{\textsf{DerivBit}=\mathbf{1}[,|L|>0,]}]
This is your controller bit: it gates whether the kernel is drift-dominated or change-dominated.
Canonical base probabilities from the casting physics (yarrow)

If you treat lines as independent under this model, then:[|L|\sim \textsf{Binomial}(6,0.25)]which yields:
k=0: 0.1779785
k=1: 0.3559570
k=2: 0.2966309
k=3: 0.1318359
k=4: 0.0329590
k=5: 0.0043945
k=6: 0.0002441
(That distribution is your default вҖңmovement weight profileвҖқ when no other discriminators are supplied.)

near sextile nexus points (multiples of 60В°), you increase the вҖңtunnel/change weightвҖқ because the 12 and 18 clocks are phase-locked there (вҖңsextile = intersection operatorвҖқ).
